SHALOM!!! Many of you have traded with me already and its been a hell of run. For those who have not just wanted to introduce my trading style so we get off to a hot start. My strategy is very outside the box..we are aiming for specific time slots especially that last 30 mins where plays run 100-2000%. Please read my alerts I will specify if we are looking for a scalp or if I recommend holding. My strategy is also very lucrative if you are just scalping 10-15% and getting out! [3/1/2026 9:39 PM] richydubz
@everyone Good evening OWLs,

I’ve been sharing my trade ideas here since we all got liberated last year, shortly after the tariff lows. I’m primarily a reversal trader who targets key liquidity levels to capture high R:R setups. My focus is on major levels, VPA, and market pain points to identify potential tops and bottoms.

My plan is usually mapped out the night before, and my entry model is strict. While I may track several ideas at once, it ultimately comes down to intraday confirmation to determine whether a trade is worth taking that day. Because of this, I’ll sometimes follow a setup for days, even weeks, waiting for the right signal.

Some of you may remember the first idea I shared shortly after joining: ENPH puts on 06/16. Since then, I’ve posted trade ideas each month in names such as MU, WMT, NKE, GOOG, BE, ARM, BABA, CMG, IBM, GLD etc...

More recently, Members Plays will remember:

GLXY (243% in 5 days), BE calls, AVGO puts, ENPH calls, IONQ puts and CRWV calls (swung over the same weekend for 120%+ and 200%+ respectively), NVDA puts off 190, INTC puts off 50, MSFT puts off both 490 and 480 -- and just last week, JPM calls and UNH puts, which returned 120% and 300% respectively on a one-day hold.

There are many other examples — I encourage anyone interested to review my post history in both main channels. Look at the setups posted, note the timestamps, and study how the charts played out afterward. That’s the clearest way to understand my approach to the markets.

{Reactions}
🔥 (58) ❤️ (26) 😂 (3) 👏 (8) 👀 (4)

[3/1/2026 9:39 PM] richydubz
This strategy naturally leads to fewer alerts. It’s also how the collaboration with Ximes developed, who trades 0DTE almost daily. We’ve known each other for years and coincidentally reconnected in OWLs last fall. Over the following weeks and months, we began noticing confluence between his trading style and my level-based, pain-point-driven approach — particularly across NQ, ES, QQQ, and SPY. From there, we refined the overlap and built on it. We share a similar mental approach to the market, and our technical frameworks blended seamlessly.

[3/11/2026 10:45 PM] followthewhiterabblt
As promised I wanted to share my thoughts with you going into this week and the why behind taking longer dated puts. I am typically a very short term 0dte-5dte trader so taking puts in April is out of character.  A few things obviously aside from the war. We are coming off of a once in a lifetime run on metals, meaning A LOT of money moved and re-shuffled. Some banks had to be on the opposite side of these trades judging by the size of the squeeze and the volume in that sector. I noticed banks (WAL, ZION, etc) did not immediately react but I came into this spring constantly watching them to see if there is signs of stress due to being short SLV. I did not expect the private credit crisis to emerge at the same time as this. SO, I was already bias  AND LOOKING for clues of weakness due to SLV then this 2nd major risk factor came into play. We are coming off of MONSTER earnings from tech, and perhaps most importantly retail has historically NEVER been as bullish and positioned in the market in the way that they are now. THEN.. we get the big war everybody has been worried about.. although most felt like would eventually happen. Now this is the piece that gave me the most confidence to get in early.. and hold through some major upside moves. The last conflict USA was involved with in Venezuela.. similar story line.. regime change.. oil.. etc. The market absolutely ripped off of that it was quick, the US benefits with the oil, a WIN for the market. Many many traders expected Iran to be the same.. and maybe even US officials were convinced it would be significantly easier/faster than what we are seeing.

[3/12/2026 9:11 AM] richydubz
@everyone NQ/ES 1HR -- We are right back within the channel we've been stuck in for months essentially going no where again, every breakout to either side of of the major channel between 24,710 and 25,250 has been a false on and quickly reverted back to the mean. You can buy the lows and sell the highs this has not been an ideal swing trading market lately. We had sick overnight holds of that 24,710 overnight low as well which is when the bounce came in.

The battleground today is between NQ holding 24,710 and ES potentially flipping a major demand into supply if it fails 6771.50, which is what it's currently doing in the pre-market. These key levels were posted Monday and continue to be a great way to frame your trades and approach the market. We NEED to see some sort of resolution between that. In a bullish market we want the NASDAQ to lead, so ideally we can continue to hold 24,710 today and push us higher. 

With that said, and for those of you who prefer to track QQQ/SPY we have to all be watching how price reacts at SPY $670.93 and QQQ $599.24 (We'll call it 600). 

Let's hope we aren't stuck in this channel for the next 3 years and can get some real swings going.

@everyone Respecting the levels kept us safe and profitable yesterday. We are testing one of the more crucial demand zones we need to see the bulls hold, we're talking prior liquidation lows from October, November, Feb, and March across ES and NQ Futures and after the failed breakdown on March 9th and making a new lower low this AM we shouldn't put a ton of weight on the bulls stepping up here until you see a shift in the intraday price action because we're certainly not getting that in the pre-market. 

Many of the levels have not changed since yesterday, and we had some extremely clean reads marking the high of day off the pain point VWAP on NQ, I posted about this in pre-market and live while it was happening. The calls we're in at the time was playing a quick gap fill and watching for failures of this level but the bulls couldn't even get there, this marked the HOD where one of the best call entries of the day was off 6715.75 when Ximes killed the entry the second it started to wick off, this level then broke and retested to give us further downside.

If you were uncomfortable shorting the highs on the open at this NQ zone, your next best opportunity came at the break and retest short of the ES 6592.75 level, which was also the SPY 651.39 and QQQ 580.25 (Which also had nice rejections at 582.04 to edge out slightly more R:R to the downside. I'm not saying you need to scalp or trade every level, but they will help define the day for you (Especially on retests). Seeing those failures come in at 24,215.50 should have hopefully got you short or had you de-risk your longs, that's the entire approach, and then again after seeing continuation breakdowns and retest failures of the levels on SPY/ES to signal for downside to come. It was an easy day to define with no headlines ripping us back in the opposite direction and the levels on all 4 were clean, we had support on SPY/QQQ for scalps long in the morning, then the longer term rejection failures to the downside signaled by all 4.

[3/31/2026 4:29 PM] followthewhiterabblt
ALRIGHT. Great day, as promised- the reason I was so confident in the longs was because #1 obviously we were way oversold. But more importantly- seeing futures last night I couldn't help but notice the amount of people on X and in here who were ready to short the pop.. and why not? It has been the move for as long as we can remember. One of my favorite setups is when people start to feel like the trade is "easy" .. once you get into that territory 90% of the time.. you are about to get fucked. In the morning I told myself if we see an aggressive sell first 5-10 mins that would be the first clue that my thesis may hold up. This got bought up instantly. But notice, we went very conservative with our strike prices and avoided 0dte. We did that for a reason. Why trap the bears when you can trap both? - That's where the 2nd sell off comes into play around 10:30- (this was the point in the day where I was 99% confident calls were going to absolutely juice) . Bears got over excited and you can tell by the velocity of that snap back.. shorts were not going to work today. That is also I believe around the time where I loaded up the cash account.

We failed the highs and continued failing into close where we chopped into the Iran announcement at 9pm where we briefly pushed and failed that major NQ level again of 24,215.50 signaling risk off until we can find that bounce. Failing 25,215.50 was the key and has been one of the most important levels on the market for weeks to define risk around. 

Now let's frame today, we need to react accordingly to how the market responds to ES 6483.50 and NQ 23,574 as these are still major supports. Take a look at NQ's channel in between 23,574 and 23,772.50, you'll see this major flip on the market as we are currently under and failing the supply above. I added yellow arrows to highlight this movement as this will be a level you need to be cautious going into and initiating new longs this morning. We are on a massive gap down and unfortunately this retest is coming in the pre-market so we'll have to see where we open up before getting aggressive with new money shorts or longs, but this is the key channel to focus on today and manage risk within.

We have net-selling on the week as even the Sunday Buyers are underwater and we'll want to track this orange VWAP within the large channel today for tradable opportunities also.

[4/8/2026 8:59 AM] richydubz
@everyone Yesterday NQ 24,266.75 rejected beautifully off open and led to a nice and easy downside move. The first bounce came off last Sunday's pain point which then found the bottom beautifully off SPY 651.39. This took us back into the next key level above again at NQ 24,266.75 for more scalp shorts, but as we all know into the bigger picture of calls that ripped into close. I stressed the key demand and bigger picture yesterday morning being SPY $651.39 for bullish continuation and price __perfectly__, and I do mean perfectly, tapped that and bounced yesterday. This is why I watch all 4 intraday every single day, we had levels to fade (Which you could use to hedge) and knew the spot that needed to hold to remain convicted on the 04/09 calls for that bigger picture move.

Today QQQ, ES & SPY have been consolidating in the pre-market above another key level nicely which should be watched for some continuation. NQ does have a potential rejection point that's seen some weakness in pre-market at 25,210.50 but as long as QQQ 607.96, ES 6822.25 demand zone, and SPY 674.88 hold us up these can be good spots to look for minor pullback points to long. After such a massive gap up I'm usually not adding too aggressively though and would caution against ruining any swing profits getting aggressive on that side off open. 

It's a massive gap up, but we are right back into the sideways channel of death we were stuck in for the months prior to selling off, I wouldn't expected us to move through this zone too easily.

The only level where price chopped more than respected was the ES 6822.25 supply, I'm going to keep this zone on the charts today in spite of yesterday from 6808.50 -> 6822.25 as this is still an important pivot the SPY/ES needs to flip. This level marked the downside on a failed retest on __03/18__ which led to nearly a **7% downside move**, prior to that it was __major lows from Feb '26, Dec '25, November '25, and a a few days in October as well__.  

On top of those normal charts, I also want to get your eyes on GC (Gold) and CL (Oil) since the chart levels are extremely clean and yesterday we saw Gold put in a daily break and retest to the downside failing 4888 on elevated volume. CL is my VIX and I have alerts set on both sides of the channel between 91.05 and 101.76. 

And if any of you remember the "SOXL vs SOXX" chart from a few months back where I pointed out how this has continuously marked the top of the semi cycle for the last half decade, and it then led to months of downside on the market as well. Well SOXL is also going to retest $70 again, and this is typical these tops because a double top on the weekly chart was the ultimate kiss of death for that cycle, and here we are again. We need to pay attention to all of these.

@everyone Yesterday we opened into the ES supply at 6822.25 which kept us from getting long off the open, the battleground was set between that and SPY $674.68. After the undercut of this level and we saw the volume come in we took profit on the shorts into @XImEs  gorgeous bottom (No pun intended but still no booty pics AFAIK 😂 ). Aggressive longs could have took calls here or off the first break and retest of 674.68, but this was the yolo move as we were still under the 6822.25 supply but it was clean none the less. The cleanest and BEST long came on the perfect break and retest of 6822.25 at 11:30 which led to the largest upside move of the day before capping off the HOD at NQ 25,257. 

Today we have much of same carrying over from yesterday, SMH/SOXX are at all time highs and you're going to want to focus more on longing to pullback to support rather than shorting the highs. 

🎯  Be patient, read the price action and let the levels tell you where we're going, no need to guess.

[4/12/2026 9:50 PM] followthewhiterabblt
@everyone  wanted to clarify my position on the market here so there is no confusion. I am not bearish on this market even with the recent headlines .. My focus is to play a short term target of around 668.44 on SPY and then flip back into longs. I was going to type out a long ass message but I think my AI did a much better job; 
 SPY Monday Setup — What I'm Watching

Friday close was euphoric. Ceasefire hopes were running high, Nasdaq up 8 days straight, everyone leaning long into the weekend.

Then the news dropped after close. Naval blockade. Peace talks collapsed. Oil +8% overnight above $100.

Here's the thing — nobody had time to react. Options markets were closed all weekend. The bears who got squeezed out during the Apr 8 ceasefire rally never got a chance to reload. The crowd at Friday close was long, not short. That changes everything about how Monday plays out.

---

What I expect:

9:30-9:50 AM — Messy open. People who bought the ceasefire rally are sellers. Initial drop toward $670. This isn't the real move — it's trapped longs getting out.

10:00 AM — Watch closely. Blockade enforcement begins. This is when the market decides which script it's running.

$670 is the obvious line. Which is exactly why I don't trust it. There's a real support level sitting at $668.44 just below it. Classic setup: break the obvious level, sweep the stops, then reverse hard while everyone who just loaded puts at $670 is underwater.

---

The two scenarios:

Scenario A (sweep & recover):
$670 breaks at 10 AM on blockade news → flushes to $668.44 → snaps back above $670 within minutes → squeeze begins. Target: $677 → $685.

Scenario B (real break):
$668.44 doesn't hold. Volume keeps building on the downside. Next stop: $659 gap fill → $651.

---

How to tell the difference in real time:

Watch the speed and volume at $668.44. A fake break dries up instantly — the selling just stops. A real break keeps volume building on every bounce attempt.

Also watch oil. If crude is still above $105 at 10 AM — the break is probably real. If oil is fading from its overnight spike — the sweep-and-recover is the play.

---

The bigger picture:

Peak cash holdings. Fear gauge above 2008 levels last week. Short interest at multi-year highs. That's a wall of worry — and walls of worry are what bull moves climb.

Markets don't reward the obvious trade. Everyone waiting for the war drop on Monday morning at 10 AM is the obvious trade.

The question isn't whether the bear case is logical. It clearly is. The question is whether the market is about to be rational — and it rarely is when sentiment is this one-sided.

---
